Jamison Brereton

20 (316)
Indra
V─Бmadeva Gautama
11 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh
The general pattern of an invitation/journey hymn is followed here. IndraтАЩs journey to our sacrifice is treated in the first two verses, with his attendance at the sacrifice and acceptance of the offerings found in the following two (3тАУ4). The invitation is summarized in verse 5. His reciprocal obligation to give generously to his worship
ers dominates the rest of the hymn, and without overt mention of the Vala myth, the poet repeatedly likens IndraтАЩs acts of giving to his opening of the cowpen and releasing its contents (vss. 6, 8, 9). A subtle reference to the Vr╠еtra myth may be found in verse 7: no тАЬobstructorтАЭ (varta╠Бr) keeps Indra from giving, using the root vr╠е
тАЬobstruct,тАЭ found in Vr╠еtra, whose name is literally тАЬobstacle.тАЭ
The hymn several times uses gambling vocabulary (vss. 3, 8), and there are some other striking images, such as the two similes in the first half of verse 5.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Indra The midsection of this hymn (vss. 5-8) has a surprising concentration of -tarstem nominals, both root- and suffix-accented.

рдЕрднрд┐рд╖реНрдЯрд┐рдХреГрддреН рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирд╕рдВрдмрдиреНрдзрд┐рдирд╛рдорднреАрд╖реНрдЯрд╛рдирд╛рдВ рдХрд░реНрддрд╛ рдЙрдЧреНрд░рдГ рддреЗрдЬрд╕реНрд╡реА рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдГ рдирдГ рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдХрдореН рдЕрд╡рд╕реЗ рд░рдХреНрд╖рдгрд╛рдп рджреВрд░рд╛рддреН рдЖ рдпрд╛рд╕рддреН рдЖрдпрд╛рддреБ рдЖрдЧрдЪреНрдЫрддреБ ред рдЕрдкрд┐ рдЪ рдЖрд╕рд╛рддреН рдЖрд╕рдиреНрдирд╛рджрдиреНрддрд┐рдХрд╛рдЪреНрдЪ рдирдГ рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдХрдорд╡рд╕реЗ рд░рдХреНрд╖рдгрд╛рдп рдЖ рдпрд╛рд╕рддреН рдЖрдпрд╛рддреБ ред рдХреАрджреГрд╢рдГ ред рд╕рдорддреНрд╕реБ рд╕рдВрдЧреНрд░рд╛рдореЗрд╖реБ рд╕рдВрдЧреЗ рд╢рддреНрд░реБрднрд┐рдГ рд╕рдВрдпреЛрдЧреЗ рд╕рддрд┐ рдкреГрддрдиреНрдпреВрдиреН рд╢рддреНрд░реВрдиреН рддреБрд░реНрд╡рдгрд┐рдГ рд╣рд┐рдВрд╕рдиреН рд╡рдЬреНрд░рдмрд╛рд╣реБрдГ рд╡рдЬреНрд░рд╣рд╕реНрддрдГ рдиреГрдкрддрд┐рдГ рд╡реГрд╖реНрдЯрд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рд░рд╛ рдиреГрдгрд╛рдВ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛рдгрд╛рдВ рдкрд╛рд▓рдХрдГ рдУрдЬрд┐рд╖реНрдареЗрднрд┐рдГ рдЕрддрд┐рд╢рдпреЗрди рддреЗрдЬрд╕реНрд╡рд┐рднрд┐рдГ рдорд░реБрджреНрднрд┐рд░реНрдпреБрдХреНрдд рдЗрддрд┐ рд╢реЗрд╖рдГ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay the illustrious Indra, the granter of desires, come to us, whether from afar or nigh, for our protection; he who is the lord of men, armed with the thunderbolt, overcoming his foes in conflict and in combats, (attended) by the most illustrious (Maruts).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Here to us from afar and here to us from nearby will powerful Indra drive for help, creating his own superiorityтАФ
the lord of men with the mace in his arm, with his most powerful (men) overcoming battlers in combat and conflicts.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Note the patterned phonological repetition d┼лr─Б╠Бd тАж ─Бs─Б╠Бd тАж y─Бsad, with the 1st two morphologically parallel (ablative sg.) and the last not (subjunctive, 3rd sg.).

To make the tr. clearer, тАЬourтАЭ should be inserted before тАЬhelp.тАЭ Otherwise it sounds as if Indra needs to find help for himself.

Griffith

FROM near or far away may mighty Indra giver of succour, come for our protection
Lord of men, armed with thunder, with the Strongest, slaying his foes in conflict, in the battles.

Geldner

Von fern und nah soll uns Indra zur Hilfe kommen, der ├Ьberlegenheit verleiht, der Gewaltige mit den gewaltigsten Mannen, der M├дnnerf├╝rst mit der Keule im Arm, der im Treffen, in den Schlachten die Angreifer ├╝berwindet.

Grassmann

Es komme Indra uns von nah und ferne zu H├╝lfe her, der m├дchtige Besch├╝tzer, Den Blitz im Arm, der Herrscher mit den St├дrksten, die Feinde zwingend bei dem Kampf in Schlachten.

Elizarenkova

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдЕрдм рдЧреНрдпрд╛рд░рд╣ рдЛрдЪрд╛рд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ рдмреАрд╕рд╡реЗрдВ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдХрд╛ рдкреНрд░рд╛рд░рдореНрдн рд╣реИ, рдЙрд╕рдХреЗ рдкреНрд░рдердо рдордиреНрддреНрд░ рдореЗрдВ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдкрджрд╡рд╛рдЪреНрдп рд░рд╛рдЬрдЧреБрдгреЛрдВ рдХреЛ рдХрд╣рддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ реерезрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рд░рд╛рдЬрдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдЬрдирд╛ ! рдпреЛрд╜рднрд┐рд╖реНрдЯрд┐рдХреГрджреНрд╡рдЬреНрд░рдмрд╛рд╣реБрд░реБрдЧреНрд░реЛ рдиреГрдкрддрд┐рд╕реНрддреБрд░реНрд╡рдгрд┐рд░рд┐рдиреНрджреНрд░ рдУрдЬрд┐рд╖реНрдареЗрднрд┐рд╕реНрд╕рд╣ рдиреЛрд╜рд╡рд╕реЗ рджреВрд░рд╛рджрд╛рд╕рд╛рджреНрд╡рд╛рд╜рд╜рдпрд╛рд╕рддреНрд╕рдорддреНрд╕реБ рдкреГрддрдиреНрдпреВрдиреНрдиреЛрд╜рд╕реНрдорд╛рдиреН рд╕рдЩреНрдЧ рдЖрдпрд╛рд╕рддреН рд╕реЛрд╜рд╕реНрдорд╛рднрд┐рд╕реНрд╕рджреИрд╡ рд░рдХреНрд╖рдгреАрдпрдГ рд╕рддреНрдХрд░реНрддреНрддрд╡реНрдпрд╢реНрдЪ реерезрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдЖ) рд╕рдордиреНрддрд╛рддреН (рдирдГ) рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдиреН (рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдГ) рдкрд░рдореИрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдпреНрдпрд╡рд╛рдиреН рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛ (рджреВрд░рд╛рддреН) (рдЖ) (рдирдГ) рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдХрдорд╕реНрдорднреНрдпрдВ рд╡рд╛ (рдЖрд╕рд╛рддреН) рд╕рдореАрдкрд╛рддреН (рдЕрднрд┐рд╖реНрдЯрд┐рдХреГрддреН) рдЕрднреАрд╖реНрдЯрд╕реБрдЦрдХрд╛рд░реА (рдЕрд╡рд╕реЗ) рд░рдХреНрд╖рдгрд╛рджреНрдпрд╛рдп (рдпрд╛рд╕рддреН) рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдиреБрдпрд╛рддреН (рдЙрдЧреНрд░рдГ) рддреЗрдЬрд╕реНрд╡реА (рдУрдЬрд┐рд╖реНрдареЗрднрд┐рдГ) рдЕрддрд┐рд╢рдпреЗрди рдмрд▓рд╛рджрд┐рдЧреБрдгрдпреБрдХреНрддреИрд░реНрдирд░реЛрддреНрддрдорд╕реИрдиреНрдпреИрдГ (рдиреГрдкрддрд┐рдГ) рдиреГрдгрд╛рдВ рдкрд╛рд▓рдХрдГ (рд╡рдЬреНрд░рдмрд╛рд╣реБрдГ) рд╡рдЬреНрд░рдГ рд╢рд╕реНрддреНрд░рд╡рд┐рд╢реЗрд╖реЛ рдмрд╛рд╣реМ рдпрд╕реНрдп рд╕рдГ (рд╕рдЩреНрдЧреЗ) рд╕рд╣ (рд╕рдорддреНрд╕реБ) рд╕рдЩреНрдЧреНрд░рд╛рдореЗрд╖реБ (рддреБрд░реНрд╡рдгрд┐рдГ) рд╢реАрдШреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░реА (рдкреГрддрдиреНрдпреВрдиреН) рдЖрддреНрдордирдГ рдкреГрддрдирд╛рдВ рд╕реЗрдирд╛рдорд┐рдЪреНрдЫреВрдиреН реерезрее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay Indra, looking down upon us, come with his steeds to our presence for our protection and enrichment; may the mighty thunderer, the possessor of wealth, (aiding us) in battle, be present at this our sacrifice.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Yajus. 20.48,49: balaiс╕е is used for marudbhiс╕е; v─Бjas─Бtau also means, for the sake of bestowing food

Jamison Brereton

Here to us let Indra drive with his fallow bays, right here, turned our way for help and benefit.
He will standтАФthat mace-bearing, bounteous one, conferring
abundanceтАФbeside this sacrifice of ours at the gaining of prizes.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Again, тАЬourтАЭ should be inserted before тАЬhelp.тАЭ

Griffith

May Indra come to us with Tawny Coursers, inclined to us, to favour and enrich us.
May Maghavan, loud-voiced and wielding thunder, stand by us at this sacrifice, in combat.

Geldner

Es komme Indra her mit seinen F├╝chsen recht nahe uns zum Helfen und zum Schenken; Der starke Blitzer, der gewalt’ge, nehme an diesem Opfer Theil bei unserm Wettkampf.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYou, Indra, plural cing us before you, shall receive this sacrifice, our holy offering; and as the huntsman (kills his game), may we, your worshippers, holder of the thunderbolt, for the acquisition of riches through you to be victorious in battle.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Setting this sacrifice of ours in front, o Indra, you will gain our intention. Like (a gambler) with the best throw to gain the stakes, with you, o
mace-bearer, might we win the contest with the stranger.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As Geldner suggests, the imagery in the first hemistich seems to come from chariot racing. P─Бda b is identical to V.31.11d (save for the ps. of the verb), a verse concerned with the chariot contest between Indra and the Sun. Putting smthg in front must simply refer to placing it in the lead, but in a ritual context like this one, there is interference between that sense and the ritual action of placing the offering fire to the east, also expressed by pur├бs тИЪdh─Б and regularly represented by the epithet of Agni pur├│hita-. But since Indra is never the agent of that ritual action and since it is the fire, not the sacrifice, that is put in front ritually, the chariot race interpr. must be primary here. In saying this, I find myself in disagreement with Bloomfield, who says тАЬThe repeated p─Бda fits well in 4.20.3, is dubious in 5.31.11,тАЭ without commenting on either the fit or the dubiousness.

The Engl. phrase тАЬgain our intentionтАЭ is somewhat awk. What saniс╣гyasi kr├бtuс╣Г naс╕е means, I think, is that IndraтАЩs action of putting the sacrifice in front will cause him to win the race, which is what we want to happen. But objects of the root тИЪsan are usually concrete (v─Б╠Бjam, etc., as in v─Б╠Бjas─Бtau in 2d; cf. also san├бye dh├гn─Бn─Бm тАЬto gain the stakesтАЭ in the next p─Бda) and also things that the grammatical subject desires to win, so my suggested indirect benefit is somewhat anomalous. So it is possible that тАЬour kr├бtuтАЭ that Indra will win is something he wants – perhaps our intention or resolve to sacrifice to him, not to other gods.

Griffith

Thou, honouring this our sacrifice, O Indra, shalt give us strength and fill us full of courage.
To win the booty, Thunder-armed! like hunters may we with thee subdue in fight our foemen.

Geldner

Wenn du diesem Opfer von uns den Vorzug gibst, wirst du unsere Absicht erreichen. Um wie ein Gl├╝cksspieler Sch├дtze zu gewinnen, wollen wir durch dich den Wettstreit des Nebenbuhlers siegreich bestehen, o Keulentr├дger.

Grassmann

Dies unser Opfer werth du haltend, Indra, wirst T├╝chtigkeit du uns verleihn, o Blitzer, Gut zu gewinnen, wie beim Spiel der W├╝rfler, lass du uns treue siegen in dem Kampfe.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬIndra, the giver of food, be near to us, favourably disposed; and anxious for our (good), drink of the effused, prepared, exhilarating Soma, and be plural ased by the (sacrificial) food (offered with the noon-day hymn.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Samandhas─Б mamadaс╕е pс╣Ыс╣гс╣нhyena: pс╣Ыс╣гс╣нhyam = m─Бdhyandinasavana udg─Бtс╣Ыbhir udg─лyam─Бnam stotram

Jamison Brereton

Being eager and of favorable mind in our midst, now (drink) of the well-pressed soma, o autonomous one.
Drink, Indra, of the honey brought before you. You will reach complete exhilaration with the soma-stalk coming from the back (of the
mountain).

Jamison Brereton Notes

The verb p─Б╠Б(с╕е) opening the 2nd half-vs. should also be read with (or supplied with) p─Бda b. Geldner supplies тАЬseiтАЭ for the first hemistich and construes the gen. phrase in b with up─Бk├й. This is possible but, given the parallelism of the two genitive phrases referring to soma in b and c, less likely.

Geldner and Witzel Got┼Н take pс╣Ыс╣гс╣нhy├а- lit. тАШrelated to the backтАЩ as an adjective of (superior) quality in a spatial metaphor – the sense of тАЬtopтАЭ in Cole PorterтАЩs тАЬYouтАЩre the topтАЭ or the adj. тАЬtip-top.тАЭ Cf. Witzel Got┼НтАЩs тАЬam erstklassigen Soma-Spross.тАЭ I think rather that the adj. is meant literally to refer to the soma plantтАЩs well-known growing place, the back of the mountains (that is, the high slopes). Cf., e.g., V.36.2 r├║hat s├│mo n├б p├бrvatasya prс╣гс╣н╠е h├й тАЬas the soma-plant grows on the back of the mountain.тАЭ

Griffith

Loving us well, benevolent, close beside us, drink, Godlike Indra, of the wellpressed Soma.
Drink of the meath we offer, and delight thee with food that cometh from the mountain ridges.

Da du Verlangen tr├дgst, sei fein wohlgemut bei unserem wohlgepre├Яten Soma, du Selbstherrlicher. Trink, Indra, von dem angebotenen S├╝├Яtrank, berausche dich mit an dem blumigen Saft!

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬLike a man boasting of his wife, I glorify that Indra who is invoked of many, who is hymned by recent sages (who is) like a tree with ripe fruit, like a victorious (warrior), skilful in arms.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

He who abounds in new seers like a fruited tree, who is a winner like a man with a sickle,
much-invoked Indra do I invite here, setting my mind on him like a
dashing youth on a maiden.

Jamison Brereton Notes

In my opinion, the first half-vs. consists of two separate similes, the second of which, sс╣Ы╠Бс╣Зyo n├б j├йt─Б, needs to be fleshed out. In the first one Indra with his abundant seers is like a tree with ripe fruit (vс╣Ыkс╣г├│ n├б pakv├бс╕е). In the second Indra the winner/conquerer is like a man who harvests the fruit with a sickle – or more likely who harvests grain, the crop having subtly changed, with the pakv├б- тАШripenedтАЩ held constant. Cf. X.101.3 n├йd─лya ├нt srс╣З╠е y├ас╕е pakv├бm ├йy─Бt тАЬthe ripe (grain) should come even closer to our sickles.тАЭ For ripe grain see I.66.3 y├бvo n├б pakv├│ j├йt─Б j├бn─Бn─Бm тАЬRipe like grain, a conquerer of peoples,тАЭ which also contains j├йtar-, though in my view in an independent syntagm.

The simile in the 2nd half-vs. is striking because it casts Indra as a maiden (y├│с╣г─Бm), pursued by the poet as a dashing and virile young man (m├бrya-, a word sometimes applied to Indra) – a notable gender reversal. This vs. contains one of the few finite forms of the secondary root тИЪrap┼Ы тАШteem, aboundтАЩ, and 2c has an occurrence of the better-attested related possessive adj.

virap┼Ы├нn-. In the currently favored etym. the тАЬrootтАЭ тИЪrap┼Ы was extracted ultimately from the nominal virap┼Ы├б- тАШabundanceтАЩ (the basis for virap┼Ы├нn-), itself constructed from a dvandva of v─лr├б- тАШmenтАЩ and pa┼Ы├║- тАШbeastsтАЩ (see EWA s.v. virap┼Ы├б-). ItтАЩs important to note, however, that this etym. is soundly rejected by K├╝mmel (417-18), though I still favor it. The two forms of the thematic pres. rap┼Ыa- (IV.45.1, X.113.2) are both immediately preceded by the preverb v├н, which (by most lights) has been secondarily extracted from the cmpd. Our perfect form here, rarap┼Ы├й, is also construed with v├н, but with y├бс╕е intervening, and the other pf. form (VI.18.12) lacks v├н but appears with pr├б in distant tmesis.

Griffith

Him who is sung aloud by recent sages, like a ripe-fruited tree, a scythe-armed victor,-
I, like a bridegroom thinking of his consort, call hither Indra, him invoked of many;

Geldner

Der ├Ьberflu├Я hat an neuen Rishi┬┤s, wie ein reifer Baum, wie ein Sichelmann, der Sieger. Wie ein Junggeselle, dessen Sinn nach einer jungen Frau steht, lade ich dich, den vielgerufenen Indra, ein.

Grassmann

Ihn, der mit neuen S├дngern reich versehn ist, gleich reifem Baum, wie Schnitter bei der Ernte, Den vielgerufnen Indra ruf’ ich zu mir, sowie der Mann die Gattin voll Verlangen.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬHe who is vast and self-sustained like a mountain, the radiant and formidable Indra, born of old for the destruction (of the foes of the gods), the wielder of the ancient thunderbolt, charged with splendour, like a jar (filled) with water.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

He who is self-strong like a mountain, lofty and powerful Indra, born from of old for conquest,
he splits open the *cowpen as a fearsome (wild beast) does a sturdy
(pen), (the pen) overflowing with goods like a bucket with water.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The published translation reflects the emendation of v├бjraс╣Г to *vraj├бс╣Г, in concert with Grassmann, Geldner, Schmidt (Bс╣Ыhaspati und Indra, 137), Lubotsky, and, after some resistance, Oldenberg The resulting phrase ─Б╠Бdart─Б *vraj├бm has a close parallel in VI.66.8 vraj├бс╣Г d├бrt─Б, as Geldner points out.

Geldner takes *vraj├бm as part of the simile and supplies Vala as the object in the frame: тАЬтАж erbricht wie einen festen Pferch (den Vala)тАжтАЭ But the position of the simile marker n├б speaks against this. I instead take *vraj├бm as a reference to Vala, with the simile portraying the attack of a wild beast (bh─лm├бс╕е) on a real pen (thus effectively reading *vraj├бm twice and separating bh─лm├бс╕е from Indra). For bh─лm├б- as a wild beast see mс╣Ыg├│ n├б bh─лm├бс╕е (I.154.2, 190.3), siс╣Гh├│ n├б bh─лm├бс╕е (IV.16.4 [nearby], IX.97.28), etc. In their tr. Witzel Got┼Н keep the transmitted text and tr. тАЬDer Furchtbare ist der die Keule Stiebende (in den) тАж prallen (Pferch) тАж,тАЭ thus silently incorporating a *vraj├бm in the final parenthesis (тАЬPferchтАЭ). I am also not certain what the VP тАЬdie Keule stiebenтАЭ would mean nor how (─Б╠Б) тИЪdс╣Ы can mean тАШstiebenтАЩ. They acknowledge the generally accepted emendation in their notes. Although I do not see an easy way to avoid this emendation, I do not know how the corruption could have arisen, esp. given vraj├бm apavart─Б╠Бsi in 8b. Still, v├бjra- is considerably more common than vraj├б- and would always be lurking in an Indra context.

Griffith

Him who in native strength is like a mountain, the lofty Indra born or old for conquest,
Terrific wielder of the ancient thunder. filled full with splendour as a jar with water.

Geldner

Der selbststark wie ein Berg, reckenhaft, von alters schon zum Siegen geboren ist, der gewaltige Indra, der Furchtbare, erbricht wie einen festen Pferch den Vala, der von Gut gedr├╝ckt voll ist wie der Sch├╢pfeimer von Wasser:

Grassmann

Urkr├дftig hoch gleich wie ein Felsen, Indra, gewaltig er, von je zur Kraft geboren, Erschliesst der hehre, uns den festen Kuhstall, ergiesst den Eimer, der mit Gut gef├╝llt ist.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬOf whom there is no opposer by (reason of) his birth nor any destroyer of the wealth that accomplishes (pious works); powerful and resplendent (Indra), the invoked of many, do you who are the showerer (of benefits) bestow upon us riches.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

For whom by nature there now exists no obstructor and no hinderer of benefit and bounty,
o strong and powerful one, boiling up and over, give riches to us, o
much invoked one.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The rel. prn. y├бsya of the first hemistich serves as a modulation pivot from the 3rd ps. of vs. 6 to the direct 2nd ps. address to Indra of 7cd.

On udv─Бvс╣Ыс╣г─Бс╣З├бс╕е see comm. ad VIII.61.7, where I reject the Neisser / Got┼Н / K├╝mmel positing of a 2nd root тИЪvarс╣г тАШsich ermannenтАЩ, etc. and assign it to тИЪvarс╣г тАШrainтАЩ, with the specialized meaning тАШboil up and overтАЩ, as an expression of irrepressible energy. This image would work nicely here with the pen тАЬoverflowing with goodsтАЭ (v├бsun─Б nyс╣Ы╠Ас╣гtam) in the preceding vs. (6d).

Griffith

Whom from of old there is not one to hinder, none to curtail the riches of his bounty.
Pouring forth freely, O thou Strong and Mighty, vouchsafe us riches, God invoked of many!

Geldner

Dessen keiner, ├╝berhaupt ein Verwehrer ist, keiner ein Hindernis seiner Freigebigkeit und Gabe. Ermann dich, du Starker, Gewaltiger, gib uns, du Vielgerufener, Reicht├╝mer!

Grassmann

Den keiner hemmt nach seiner Art, dem keiner verk├╝rzt die Gabe, die du reichlich spendest, Dich reich ergiessend, kr├дftiger, gewalt’ger, verleih uns Sch├дtze nun, o vielgerufner.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYou rule over the riches and the dwellings of men; you are the rescuer of the herd of cattle; you are the giver of the instrumental uction, the smiter in battles, and the distributor of great heaps of riches.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

You are master of wealth and of the peaceful dwelling of the settled domains, and you open the pen of cows.
Doing your best for men in the clashes, hitting the jackpot, you are the guide to an abundant heap of goods.

Jamison Brereton Notes

For brief and unilluminating comments on ┼Ыikс╣г─Бnar├б- see comm. ad I.53.2.

Here I prefer to read the loc samith├йс╣гu with it rather than with what follows.

The root noun cmpd. prah─Б╠Б- is discussed with care and insight by Scarlatta (698- 700). The cmpd. is found in X.42.9 in a clear gambling context. Of the various proposals Scarlatta makes, I find most satisfying the one in which prah─Б╠Б- is the stakes/pool/kitty тАШleft out in frontтАЩ. The possessive adj. here would then mean тАШhaving the jackpotтАЩ and would fit with the gambling imagery in 3d ┼Ыvaghn─л╠Бva тАж san├бye dh├бn─Бn─Бm тАЬlike (a gambler) with the best throw to gain the stakes.тАЭ (Scarlatta, however, takes our particular passage in a different and, to me, unconvincing direction, p.

700.) The standard interpr. is тАШtake the leadтАЩ (e.g., Geldner тАЬden Vorsprung gewinnendтАЭ) in a race, but IтАЩm not sure how this meaning would develop from тАШleaveтАЩ and тАШforthтАЩ.

Griffith

Of wealth and homes of men thou art the ruler, and opener of the stable of the cattle.
Helper of men, winner of spoil in combats, thou leadest to an ample heap of riches.

Geldner

Du verf├╝gst ├╝ber den Reichtum, ├╝ber den Wohnsitz der V├╢lker und du bist der, der den Pferch der Rinder ├╢ffnet. Den M├дnnern gern n├╝tzend, in den Schlachten den Vorsprung gewinnend, bist du der, der zu einer gro├Яen Masse von Gut f├╝hrt.

Grassmann

In deiner Hand ist Gut und Macht der Menschen, du bist es, der den Stall der K├╝he ├╢ffnet, Den Menschen spendet, Beute macht in K├дmpfen und reiche Gab’ an jedem Gut herbeif├╝hrt.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬBy what wisdom is he who is most wise renowned by that wherewith the mighty Indra repeatedly does (great things); he is the especial effacer of the manifold sin of the worshipper, and bestows wealth upon his adorer.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Because of what ability is he famed as the most able?тАФthat ability by which the lofty one does everything instantly.
He is the best at prying apart narrow straits for the man who does
much pious service, and he establishes material property for the
singer.

Jamison Brereton Notes

P─Бda a is a definitional one, with the precise type of ability (┼Ы├бc─л-) possessed by Indra giving him the designation тАШmost ableтАЩ (┼Ы├бciс╣гс╣нha).

Geldner interprets m├║hu k─Б╠Бcid as haplology for *muhuk─Б╠Бk─Б╠Бcid (so also EWA s.v. m├║hur, Witzel Got┼Н, and, somewhat differently, Oldenberg flg. Ludwig). Cf. nearby IV.16.17 k├бsmi├▒ cid тАж muhuk├й (also muhuka├нс╕е IV.17.12). I have come, somewhat reluctantly, to the conclusion that this is correct. However, as noted in disc. ad IV.16.17, I do not accept GeldnerтАЩs rendering of muhuk├б- as тАШSchlachtgeschreiтАЩ, which produces for this passage тАЬтАж jedwedes Schlachtgeschrei hervorruft.тАЭ Witzel Got┼НтАЩs тАЬтАж welches pl├╢tzlichen Vorf├дlle auch immer erledigtтАЭ is, however, more plausible. In IV.16.17 I suggest a sense тАШskirmishтАЩ, which works contextually there, but is here, I think, too specific. In fact, the published translation, тАЬdoes everything instantly,тАЭ can stand, for a literal Engl. тАЬdoes every instantaneous thing.тАЭ The lexeme v├н тИЪci means literally тАШpull apartтАЩ; an exactly parallel usage to this one appears in VI.67.8 yuv├бс╣Г d─Б┼Ы├║с╣гe v├н cayiс╣гс╣нam ├бс╣Гhaс╕е (also cited by Geldner), and the notion of pulling apart / opening up a narrow place (├бс╣Гhaс╕е) is very apposite. It should also be noted, however, that the same lexeme is used in gambling contexts, indeed in the very X.42.9 just cited for prah─Б╠Бvant- in 8c. In gambling it means тАШpile apart, pull out (a good hand)тАЩ. Although I donтАЩt think that that idiomatic sense is reflected here, I do think that the gambling overtones would resonate with the other gambling vocabulary in this hymn.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬHarm us not, but cherish us, Indra; bestow upon us that abundant wealth which it is yours to give to the donor (of the oblation); praising you, we celebrate you at this sacred rite, which is new and excellent, and (at which the oblation) is proper to be presented.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Do not neglect us! Bring and give us what of yours is to be given in abundance to the pious man.
At this new gift we shall proclaim it in this hymn recited for you,
praising you, o Indra.

Jamison Brereton Notes

I do not understand the function of the initial pr├б in b. Grassmann indicates that it belongs with d─Б╠Бtave, and Keydana (Infinitive, p. 255) explicitly says that it must belong with d─Б╠Бtave and is therefore in tmesis. Though this is not impossible, I am somewhat reluctant to accept this explanation in part because pr├б is relatively rare with тИЪd─Б. I wonder if it signals the lexeme pr├б тИЪas тАШbe present, be prominentтАЩ, with the copula gapped. Fortunately, the interpr. chosen has almost no effect on the sense of the p─Бda.

Griffith

Slay us not; bring, bestow onus the ample gift which thou hast to give to him who offers.
At this new gift, with this laud sung before thee, extolling thee, we, Indra, will declare it.

Keith

Destroy us not; bring and give to us
That plenteous bounty which thou hast to give to the pious man,
For this new gift, this song we have sung to thee;
Let us speak forth in praise of Indra.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬGlorified (in the past) glorified, Indra, at present, satisfy your worshipper with food, as rivers (are filled with water); lord of horses, a new hymn has been made for you; may we, possessed of chariots, be ever delighted in your praise.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

тАУ Now praised, O Indra, now being sung, make refreshment swell for the singer like rivers.
A new sacred formulation has been made for you, o you of the fallow bays. Through our insightful thought may we be charioteers who
always win.

Griffith

Now, Indra! lauded, glorified with praises, let power swell high, like rivers, for the singer.
A new hymn, Lord of Bays! for thee is fashioned. May we, car-born, through song be victors ever.

  • рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░:
  • рд╡рд╛рдорджреЗрд╡реЛ рдЧреМрддрдордГ

  • рдкрдЮреНрдЪрдордГ
рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдлрд┐рд░ рдЙрдкрджреЗрд╢рд╡рд┐рд╖рдп рдХреЛ рдЕрдЧрд▓реЗ рдордиреНрддреНрд░ рдореЗрдВ рдХрд╣рддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ (рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░) рд╕реБрдЦ рдХреЗ рджреЗрдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ ! (рд╕реНрддреБрддрдГ) рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рд┐рдд рд╣реБрдП рдЖрдк (рдЬрд░рд┐рддреНрд░реЗ) рд╕рддреНрдп рдХрд╣рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ рдХреЗ рд▓рд┐рдпреЗ (рдирд╡реНрдпрдореН) рдирд╡реАрди (рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдо) рдмреЬреЗ рдзрди рд╡рд╛ рдЕрдиреНрди рдХреА (рдиреБ) рд╢реАрдШреНрд░ (рдирджреНрдпрдГ) рдирджрд┐рдпреЛрдВ рдХреЗ (рди) рд╕рджреГрд╢ (рдкреАрдкреЗрдГ) рд╡реГрджреНрдзрд┐ рдХрд░реЛ рдФрд░ (рдЧреГрдгрд╛рдирдГ) рд╕реНрддреБрддрд┐ рдХрд░рддрд╛ рд╣реБрдЖ рдирд╡реАрди (рдЗрд╖рдореН) рд╡рд┐рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рди рдХреА рд╡реГрджреНрдзрд┐ рдХрд░реЛ рд╣реЗ (рд╣рд░рд┐рд╡рдГ) рдмрд╣реБрдд рд╕реЗрдирд╛ рдХреЗ рдЕрдЩреНрдЧреЛрдВ рд╕реЗ рдпреБрдХреНрдд ! рдЬрд┐рд╕рдХреЗ рд▓рд┐рдпреЗ (рддреЗ) рдЖрдкрдХреЗ рд╣рдо рд▓реЛрдЧреЛрдВ рдиреЗ (рдзрд┐рдпрд╛) рдХрд░реНрдо рд╕реЗ рдирд╡реАрди рдмреЬрд╛ рдзрди рд╡рд╛ рдЕрдиреНрди (рдЕрдХрд╛рд░рд┐) рдХрд┐рдпрд╛ рдЙрд╕рдХреЗ рд╕рд╣рд╛рдп рд╕реЗ (рд╕рджрд╛рд╕рд╛рдГ) рд╕рдорд╛рди рджрд╛рди рджреЗрдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ рд╕реЗрд╡рдХ рд╣рдо рд▓реЛрдЧ (рд░рдереНрдпрдГ) рдмрд╣реБрдд рд╕реБрдиреНрджрд░ рд░рде рдЖрджрд┐рдХреЛрдВ рд╕реЗ рдпреБрдХреНрдд (рдиреБ) рдирд┐рд╢реНрдЪрдп (рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдо) рд╣реЛрд╡реЗрдВ реерезрезрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдордиреНрддреНрд░реА, рд╕реЗрдирд╛ рдФрд░ рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдЬрдиреЛрдВ рдХреЛ рд╢реНрд░реЗрд╖реНрда рдХрд░реНрдореНрдо рдХрд░рддреЗ рд╣реБрдП рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛ рдХреА рд╕реНрддреБрддрд┐ рдЬреИрд╕реА рдХрд░реНрддреНрддрд╡реНрдп рд╣реИ, рд╡реИрд╕реА рд╣реА рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛ рдХреЛ рднреА рдЗрди рдЙрддреНрддрдо рдХрд░реНрдореНрдореЛрдВ рдореЗрдВ рдкреНрд░рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрдорд╛рди рд▓реЛрдЧреЛрдВ рдХреА рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рд╛ рдХрд░рдиреА рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдпреЗ реерезрезрее рдЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдореЗрдВ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░, рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛, рдЕрдорд╛рддреНрдп рдФрд░ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреЛрдВ рдХреЗ рдЧреБрдгреЛрдВ рдХрд╛ рд╡рд░реНрдгрди рд╣реЛрдиреЗ рд╕реЗ рдЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдХреЗ рдЕрд░реНрде рдХреА рдЗрд╕ рд╕реЗ рдкрд┐рдЫрд┐рд▓реЗ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдХреЗ рдЕрд░реНрде рдХреЗ рд╕рд╛рде рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐ рдЬрд╛рдирдиреА рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдпреЗ реерезрезрее рдпрд╣ рдмреАрд╕рд╡рд╛рдБ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдФрд░ рдЪреМрдерд╛ рд╡рд░реНрдЧ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реБрдЖ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░ ! рд╕реНрддреБрддрд╕реНрд╕рдВрд╕реНрддреНрд╡рдВ рдЬрд░рд┐рддреНрд░реЗ рдирд╡реНрдпрдореНрдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдо рдиреБ рдирджреНрдпреЛ рди рдкреАрдкреЗрдГред рдЧреГрдгрд╛рдирдГ рд╕рдиреНрдирд╡реНрдпрдорд┐рд╖рдореНрдкреАрдкреЗрдГред рд╣реЗ рд╣рд░рд┐рд╡реЛ ! рдпрд╕реНрдореИ рддреЗрд╜рд╕реНрдорд╛рднрд┐рд░реНрдзрд┐рдпрд╛ рдирд╡реНрдпрдВ рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдорд╛рд╜рдХрд╛рд░рд┐ рддрддреНрд╕рд╣рд╛рдпреЗрди рд╕рджрд╛рд╕рд╛ рд╡рдпрдВ рд░рдереНрдпреЛ рдиреБ рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдо реерезрезрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкреБрдирд░реБрдкрджреЗрд╢рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдорд╛рд╣ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдиреБ) рд╕рджреНрдпрдГ (рд╕реНрддреБрддрдГ) рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рд┐рддрдГ (рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░) рд╕реБрдЦрдкреНрд░рджрд╛рддрдГ (рдиреБ) (рдЧреГрдгрд╛рдирдГ) рд╕реНрддреБрд╡рдиреН (рдЗрд╖рдореН) рд╡рд┐рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирдореН (рдЬрд░рд┐рддреНрд░реЗ) рд╕рддреНрдпрдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рдХрд╛рдп (рдирджреНрдпрдГ) (рди) рдЗрд╡ (рдкреАрдкреЗрдГ) рд╡рд░реНрдзрдп (рдЕрдХрд╛рд░рд┐) рдХреНрд░рд┐рдпрддреЗ (рддреЗ) рддрд╡ (рд╣рд░рд┐рд╡рдГ) рдмрд╣реБрд╕реЗрдирд╛рдЩреНрдЧрдпреБрдХреНрдд (рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдо) рдорд╣рджреНрдзрдирдордиреНрдирдВ рд╡рд╛ (рдирд╡реНрдпрдореН) рдирд╡реАрдирдореН (рдзрд┐рдпрд╛) рдХрд░реНрдореНрдордгрд╛ (рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдо) (рд░рдереНрдпрдГ) рдмрд╣реБрд░рдордгреАрдпрд░рдерд╛рджрд┐рдпреБрдХреНрддрд╛рдГ (рд╕рджрд╛рд╕рд╛рдГ) рд╕рдорд╛рдирджрд╛рдирд╕реЗрд╡рдХрд╛рдГ реерезрезрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЕрдорд╛рддреНрдпрд╕реЗрдирд╛рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдЬрдиреИрдГ рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рд┐рддрд╛рдирд┐ рдХрд░реНрдореНрдорд╛рдгрд┐ рдХреБрд░реНрд╡рддреЛ рд░рд╛рдЬреНрдЮрдГ рд╕реНрддреБрддрд┐рд░реНрдпрдерд╛ рдХрд╛рд░реНрдпреНрдпрд╛ рддрдереИрд╡ рд░рд╛рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдкреНрдпреЗрддреЗрд╖рд╛рдВ рд╢реБрднрдХрд░реНрдореНрдорд╕реБ рдкреНрд░рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрдорд╛рдирд╛рдирд╛рдВ рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рд╛ рдХрд░реНрддреНрддрд╡реНрдпреЗрддрд┐ реерезрезрее рдЕрд░реНрддреЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛рд╜рдорд╛рддреНрдпрд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рджреНрдЧреБрдгрд╡рд░реНрдгрдирд╛рджреЗрддрджрд░реНрдерд╕реНрдп рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдереЗрди рд╕рд╣ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐рд░реНрд╡реЗрджреНрдпрд╛ реерезрезрее рдЗрддрд┐ рд╡рд┐рдВрд╢рддрд┐рддрдордВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рдЪрддреБрд░реНрдереЛ рд╡рд░реНрдЧрд╢реНрдЪ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрддрдГ рее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдордВрддреНрд░реА, рд╕реЗрдирд╛ рд╡ рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдЬрдирд╛рдВрдиреА рд╢реНрд░реЗрд╖реНрда рдХрд░реНрдо рдХрд░рдд рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛рдЪреА рд╕реНрддреБрддреА рдХрд░рдгреЗ рдХрд░реНрддрд╡реНрдп рд╕рдордЬрд▓реЗ рдкрд╛рд╣рд┐рдЬреЗ рддрд╕реЗрдЪ рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛рдиреЗрд╣реА рдпрд╛ рдЙрддреНрддрдо рдХрд░реНрдорд╛рдд рдЕрд╕рд▓реЗрд▓реНрдпрд╛ рд▓реЛрдХрд╛рдВрдЪреА рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рд╛ рдХреЗрд▓реА рдкрд╛рд╣рд┐рдЬреЗ. рее резрез рее
